This minimizes AWI's argument that environmental conditions "worsened" between signing and closing, reducing MAE claim probability. | MSWC General Counsel | Before signing and updated monthly through closing | Minimal (internal counsel time) |

#### E.2 Draft Contract Language

**E.2(i) - Enhanced Proxy Statement Disclosure (Risk Factors Section)**

*[Insert in MSWC Proxy Statement Section III - "Risk Factors Related to the Merger," immediately after "Risk Factors Related to MSWC's Business"]:*

**The Company faces significant environmental compliance obligations that may not be fully recoverable through customer rates and may adversely affect the value of your investment.**

The Company's water utility operations are subject to extensive federal and state environmental regulations, including the Resource Conservation and Recovery Act (RCRA), the Safe Drinking Water Act (SDWA), and regulations administered by the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) and the California Public Utilities Commission (CPUC). The Company has identified three categories of environmental non-compliance requiring substantial capital investment over the next 7-15 years:

**RCRA Hazardous Waste Management Violations.** The Company's Riverside facility (EPA ID: TX0001492837) has received Notices of Violation from the EPA for 12 consecutive quarters (Q1 2022 through Q4 2024) relating to hazardous waste storage, labeling, and disposal practices. The EPA has initiated discussions with the Company regarding entry into an Administrative Consent Order requiring: (i) immediate corrective measures to achieve RCRA compliance; (ii) third-party compliance monitoring for a period of 24-36 months; and (iii) payment of civil penalties. The Company estimates that achieving full RCRA compliance will require capital expenditures of $25 million to $50 million over the next 36 months, plus potential civil penalties ranging from $500,000 to $2 million. The Company has not yet commenced the corrective action process and has not budgeted these costs in its current five-year capital plan. There can be no assurance that the CPUC will permit the Company to recover these costs through customer rates, particularly given that the violations resulted from the Company's failure to comply with longstanding RCRA requirements rather than from new regulatory mandates.

**PFAS Contamination Remediation.** EPA testing conducted in 2020-2024 has detected per- and polyfluoroalkyl substances (PFAS) in 8 of the Company's water systems serving approximately 147,000 customer connections (31% of the Company's total service population). PFAS concentrations in these systems range from 5.2 parts per trillion (ppt) to 38 ppt, exceeding the EPA's final Maximum Contaminant Level (MCL) of 4 ppt established in April 2024. The Company is required to achieve compliance with the EPA MCLs by October 2029 (5.5 years from the effective date). The Company estimates that installing granular activated carbon (GAC) filtration systems at the 8 affected facilities will require capital expenditures with a net present value of $150 million to $230 million (assuming 5% discount rate and 30-year useful life). However, CPUC regulations generally prohibit utilities from recovering capital costs through rates if the expenditures are not included in a General Rate Case (GRC) filed within 36 months of the investment. The Company's next GRC filing deadline is January 2026. If the Company defers PFAS capital investments beyond 2029 (i.e., more than 36 months before the Company's subsequent GRC filing in 2029-2030), the Company faces a 40-60% risk that the CPUC will disallow recovery of late-incurred costs, resulting in $60 million to $140 million of unrecoverable capital expenditures that would reduce earnings and stockholder value.

**Lead Service Line Replacement.** The Company estimates that its distribution system includes approximately 148,000 lead service lines (defined as service lines with any lead components, including customer-owned portions) representing 31% of the Company's customer connections. This percentage is above the national median of 18-22% for water utilities. The EPA's final Lead and Copper Rule Improvements (LCRI), effective January 2025, require mandatory replacement of all known lead service lines within 10 years (by January 2035). The Company estimates that full system-wide lead line replacement will require capital expenditures of $1.4 billion to $1.95 billion over 10 years (approximately $140 million to $195 million annually). Historically, California water utilities have recovered only the utility-side portion of lead line replacement costs through rates (averaging 50-80% of total costs), with customers bearing the cost of replacing the customer-side portion of the service line. However, recent CPUC decisions have indicated the Commission may require utilities to bear 50% of customer-side replacement costs to ensure equitable access to safe drinking water, particularly in disadvantaged communities. If the CPUC adopts a 50% utility cost-sharing requirement for customer-side replacements, the Company's total capital obligation would increase to $1.75 billion to $2.1 billion, with $700 million to $975 million representing utility costs beyond current capital plans. There can be no assurance that the CPUC will permit full cost recovery for these expenditures, and any disallowance would reduce earnings and stockholder value.

**Aggregate Environmental Capital Exposure and Rate Recovery Risk.** The aggregate environmental capital obligations described above total $2.0 billion to $3.2 billion over the next 10-15 years, representing 83% to 133% of the merger consideration of $2.4 billion. While the Company believes that a substantial portion of these costs will be recoverable through customer rates under CPUC cost-of-service ratemaking, there can be no assurance that the CPUC will approve full cost recovery, particularly for costs resulting from the Company's delayed response to known environmental compliance obligations. The Company estimates a 40-60% probability that CPUC rate case proceedings will disallow $425 million to $1 billion of environmental CapEx recovery due to: (i) failure to comply with the 36-month GRC filing timeline for PFAS investments; (ii) customer-side lead line cost allocation disputes; (iii) CPUC's increasing scrutiny of utility management imprudence. If the CPUC disallows environmental cost recovery at the high end of this range ($1 billion), the Company's earnings would decline by approximately 35-50%, adversely affecting the value of your investment in the merger and potentially affecting AWI's ability to pay the merger consideration.

**Impact on Merger Consideration and Stockholder Value.** The Board of Directors considered the environmental compliance obligations described above when evaluating the fairness of AWI's $2.4 billion merger consideration. The Board received a fairness opinion from [Financial Advisor] opining that the merger consideration is fair to the Company's stockholders from a financial point of view, taking into account the environmental liabilities and the range of potential outcomes from CPUC rate case proceedings. However, the fairness opinion included significant assumptions regarding the probability and magnitude of CPUC cost disallowances, and actual results may differ materially from these assumptions. If environmental remediation costs exceed current estimates or if CPUC cost recovery is less favorable than assumed in the fairness opinion, the merger consideration may not adequately compensate stockholders for the diminished value of the Company's business. You should carefully consider these risks when deciding whether to vote in favor of the merger.

**Stockholder Vote Required; No Appraisal Rights Available.** Under Delaware law, approval of the merger requires the affirmative vote of holders of a majority of the Company's outstanding common stock. If you do not vote, your non-vote will have the same effect as a vote against the merger. Delaware law does not provide appraisal rights to dissenting stockholders in all-cash merger transactions where the acquiring company owns 90% or more of the outstanding stock, but because AWI currently owns 0% of the Company's stock, appraisal rights under Section 262 of the Delaware General Corporation Law are available to stockholders who properly perfect their appraisal claims. If you seek appraisal, you will not receive the $[X] per share merger consideration but instead will be entitled to receive the judicially-determined "fair value" of your shares, which may be more or less than the merger consideration depending on the court's assessment of the Company's value giving effect to the environmental liabilities described above.

*[Drafting Notes for Counsel]:*
- This disclosure is modeled on *In re Volcano Corp. Stockholder Litigation*, 143 A.3d 727, 741-43 (Del. Ch. 2016), requiring disclosure of not only regulatory non-compliance but also management's assessment of severity and likely financial impact
- Quantified ranges ($25M-$50M, $150M-$230M, $1.4B-$1.95B) based on Phase II ESA reports, EPA technical guidance, and engineering cost estimates available to management
- Probability estimates (40-60% disallowance risk) based on analysis of CPUC GRC decisions 2018-2024 showing increased scrutiny of utility management imprudence
- "Impact on Merger Consideration" section directly addresses *TSC Industries* materiality standard: would a reasonable stockholder consider this information important in deciding how to vote?
- Disclosure goes beyond generic "environmental compliance obligations exist" to provide stockholders with specific information enabling informed assessment of whether $2.4B consideration adequately values MSWC given environmental exposure

**E.2(ii) - Material Adverse Effect Definition with Environmental Carve-Out Cap**

*[Revise Merger Agreement Article 10.1(a) as follows, with new environmental-specific carve-out language in bold]:*

**Section 10.1 Material Adverse Effect.**

(a) **Definition.** "Material Adverse Effect" means any event, change, effect, development, state of facts, condition, or occurrence (each, an "**Effect**") that, individually or in the aggregate, (i) has had or would reasonably be expected to have a material adverse effect on the business, financial condition, results of operations, or prospects of the Company and its Subsidiaries, taken as a whole, or (ii) prevents, materially delays, or materially impairs the ability of the Company to consummate the transactions contemplated by this Agreement; **provided**, **however**, that "Material Adverse Effect" shall not include any Effect to the extent resulting from, arising out of, or attributable to:

(1) general economic or political conditions or changes therein, or conditions or changes in the financial, banking, or securities markets generally, including changes in interest rates, credit availability, or currency exchange rates;

(2) conditions or changes generally affecting the industries or markets in which the Company operates, including regulatory changes affecting the water utility sector generally;

(3) any outbreak, escalation, or worsening of hostilities, acts of war (whether or not declared), sabotage, terrorism, or military actions, or any escalation or worsening of any such hostilities, acts of war, sabotage, terrorism, or military actions;

(4) earthquakes, hurricanes, tsunamis, tornadoes, floods, mudslides, wildfires, or other natural disasters, weather conditions, or pandemics, epidemics, or disease outbreaks (including COVID-19 and any related Governmental Order);

(5) changes or proposed changes in GAAP or other accounting standards, or changes or proposed changes in applicable Law or the interpretation or enforcement thereof, including changes in EPA or CPUC regulations affecting water quality standards, treatment requirements, or ratemaking methodologies;

(6) any action taken (or omitted to be taken) by the Company at the request or with the consent of Buyer, or any action required to be taken by the Company under this Agreement;

(7) the announcement of this Agreement, the pendency or consummation of the transactions contemplated hereby, or the identity of Buyer, including the impact thereof on relationships, contractual or otherwise, with customers, suppliers, distributors, employees, labor unions, or Governmental Authorities (provided that this clause (7) shall not apply to the representation in Section 4.5 regarding the absence of conflicts requiring third-party consents);

(8) any failure by the Company to meet internal or published projections, forecasts, estimates, or predictions in respect of revenues, earnings, or other financial or operating metrics for any period (provided that the underlying causes of such failures shall not be excluded to the extent not otherwise excluded under this definition);

**(9)** **Environmental Compliance Costs or Capital Expenditures**, **including costs related to RCRA violations, PFAS contamination remediation, or lead service line replacement, to the extent such costs or expenditures, individually or in the aggregate**: **(i) do not exceed $200 million in any consecutive 24-month period following the Effective Date; (ii) do not result in service disruptions, customer connection outages, or boil-water notices affecting more than 25,000 customer connections at any one time; (iii) do not result in cumulative CPUC rate case disallowances exceeding $300 million in the aggregate across all General Rate Case proceedings filed during the 60-month period following the Effective Date; and (iv) do not result in the imposition of a court-appointed or EPA-appointed third-party compliance monitor with operational veto authority over the Company's capital budget or executive management decisions;**

**provided further** that, with respect to clauses (1), (2), (3), (4), and (5) above, if any such Effect has a disproportionate adverse effect on the Company and its Subsidiaries, taken as a whole, relative to other participants in the water utility industry in California, then only the incremental disproportionate impact may be taken into account in determining whether a Material Adverse Effect has occurred.

*[Drafting Notes for Counsel]:*
- **Subclause (i) ($200M Cap):** Permits environmental CapEx up to $200M per 24-month period without triggering MAE. This threshold is calibrated to the $150M-$230M PFAS NPV investment + $25M-$50M RCRA remediation = $175M-$280M total near-term CapEx. Threshold of $200M allocates risk: costs within projections are MSWC's risk; costs exceeding projections give AWI termination/price adjustment rights.
- **Subclause (ii) (25,000 Connections):** Permits service disruptions affecting up to 25,000 connections (approximately 5% of MSWC's 480,000 total connections) without MAE. This accommodates routine lead line replacement disruptions (148,000 total lines ÷ 10 years = 14,800 lines/year, phased over 12 months = 1,200 lines/month with 2-3 day disruptions per connection = 2,400-3,600 connections disrupted monthly). However, catastrophic events (system-wide contamination, major treatment plant failure) affecting >25,000 connections would constitute MAE.
- **Subclause (iii) ($300M CPUC Disallowance Cap):** Allocates rate case disallowance risk: CPUC disallowances under $300M are MSWC's risk (carved out of MAE definition), but disallowances exceeding $300M give AWI MAE rights. This threshold is calibrated to the 40-60% probability × $425M-$1B potential disallowance = $170M-$600M expected value range. The $300M cap falls near the midpoint of this range, creating balanced risk allocation.
- **Subclause (iv) (Compliance Monitor Restriction):** Carves out routine EPA/CPUC oversight from MAE scope but preserves MAE for extreme enforcement scenarios where the Company loses operational control (third-party monitor with veto authority over budget/management decisions, analogous to FDA consent decrees in *Akorn*).
- **"Disproportionately Affected" Exception:** Retains standard "disproportionately affected" language from *Snow Phipps Group, LLC v. KCAKE Acquisition, Inc.*, 2021 WL 1714202 (Del. Ch. 2021). This exception applies to general carve-outs (clauses 1-5) but NOT to the environmental-specific carve-out (clause 9), ensuring that if MSWC's environmental exposure significantly exceeds industry norms, AWI cannot claim disproportionate impact to circumvent the $200M/$300M caps. However, the environmental carve-out itself contains built-in proportionality: the $200M cap is calibrated to MSWC's specific environmental liabilities, so exceeding the cap inherently means costs are disproportionate to what was disclosed and priced at signing.
- **Negotiation Strategy:** MSWC should resist AWI's likely proposal to eliminate the carve-out caps entirely (making all environmental costs potential MAE triggers). MSWC should argue that: (a) environmental liabilities were disclosed in data room; (b) AWI conducted Phase II ESAs and reviewed EPA correspondence; (c) AWI's financial advisors valued MSWC incorporating environmental costs; therefore (d) AWI cannot claim "unknown risk" per *IBP* precedent. The capped carve-out represents a compromise: MSWC accepts that costs materially exceeding disclosed estimates may constitute MAE, but routine compliance costs within disclosed ranges are carved out.
- **Counter-Proposal from AWI:** AWI will likely propose lowering the caps to $150M (24-month CapEx), $200M (cumulative CPUC disallowances), and 15,000 customer connections. MSWC should counter that: (a) $150M cap is below the $175M-$280M disclosed PFAS+RCRA investment, making the carve-out illusory; (b) $200M CPUC disallowance cap is below the $170M-$600M expected value range, unfairly allocating risk to MSWC; (c) 15,000 connection disruption limit is below the 14,800 annual lead line replacement pace, making lead line compliance impossible without triggering MAE. MSWC should hold firm at $200M/$300M/25,000 thresholds as balanced risk allocation.

**E.2(iii) - Stockholder Approval Mechanics and Appraisal Rights Notice**

*[Insert in Merger Agreement Article 7.1(c) - Conditions Precedent to Buyer's Obligations]:*

**Section 7.1 Conditions Precedent to Buyer's Obligations.** The obligation of Buyer to consummate the Merger is subject to the satisfaction (or waiver by Buyer) of the following conditions:

[...existing conditions...]

**(c) Stockholder Approval.** This Agreement and the Merger shall have been approved and adopted by the holders of a majority of the outstanding shares of Company Common Stock in accordance with the DGCL and the Company's Certificate of Incorporation and Bylaws (the "**Stockholder Approval**"). For purposes of this Section 7.1(c):

(i) The Company shall prepare and file with the Delaware Secretary of State, and mail or deliver electronically to all holders of Company Common Stock as of the record date for the Stockholder Meeting, a proxy statement (the "**Proxy Statement**") complying with all requirements of the DGCL, including without limitation the requirement under Section 251(c) of the DGCL that notice of the Stockholder Meeting be provided at least 20 days prior to the meeting date.

(ii) The Proxy Statement shall include: (A) a copy of this Agreement or a fair summary of the material terms hereof; (B) the written opinion of the Company's financial advisor that the Merger Consideration is fair to the Company's stockholders from a financial point of view (the "**Fairness Opinion**"); (C) a description of the background of the Merger, including a summary of the process undertaken by the Company's Board of Directors in evaluating strategic alternatives and negotiating the terms of this Agreement; (D) a complete and accurate description of the appraisal rights available to dissenting stockholders under Section 262 of the DGCL, including the procedures that must be followed to perfect such rights; and (E) all other information required by applicable Law and fiduciary duties to enable the Company's stockholders to make an informed decision regarding the Merger.

(iii) The Company represents and warrants that the Proxy Statement, as of the date first mailed or delivered to stockholders and as of the date of the Stockholder Meeting, shall not contain any untrue statement of a material fact or omit to state any material fact required to be stated therein or necessary to make the statements therein, in light of the circumstances under which they were made, not misleading. The Company acknowledges that this representation is a "fundamental representation" for purposes of Article 11 (Indemnification) and that any breach of this representation shall survive Closing and shall not be subject to any monetary cap or basket.

(iv) If the Stockholder Approval is not obtained at the initial Stockholder Meeting, the Company shall, within 30 days thereafter, hold a second Stockholder Meeting after addressing stockholder concerns (which may include increasing the Merger Consideration or providing additional disclosure in a supplemental proxy statement). If the Stockholder Approval is not obtained at the second Stockholder Meeting, Buyer may elect to: (A) terminate this Agreement without penalty; or (B) waive the Stockholder Approval condition and proceed to Closing subject to satisfaction of all other conditions.

*[Drafting Notes for Counsel]:*
- Subclause (ii)(D) appraisal rights disclosure is mandated by Del. Code Ann. tit. 8, § 262(d)(2), requiring notice of appraisal rights in the proxy materials
- Subclause (iii) "fundamental representation" designation means: (a) representation survives Closing indefinitely (not subject to 18-24 month survival periods for ordinary representations); (b) breaches are not subject to $15M-$25M basket (first-dollar indemnification); (c) breaches are not subject to $200M-$400M cap (unlimited indemnification). This incentivizes MSWC to ensure proxy disclosure is complete and accurate per Finding B.1 analysis.
- Subclause (iv) contemplates two stockholder votes if first vote fails, consistent with Delaware law permitting multiple votes on same transaction unless certificate of incorporation prohibits. However, if second vote also fails, AWI can terminate without paying reverse termination fee (stockholder approval failure is a "Company Breach" under Article 10.3(b) permitting fee-free Buyer termination).

#### E.3 Pre-Closing Conditions and Action Items

| # | Condition/Action | Trigger Event | Responsible Party | Estimated Timeline |
|---|------------------|---------------|-------------------|-------------------|
| 1 | **Board Approval of Merger Agreement (or Substantially Final Form)**: MSWC Board of Directors must approve merger agreement per DGCL § 251(b). Effective August 1, 2024, new § 147 permits approval of "substantially final form" rather than complete final agreement, allowing post-approval ministerial changes without reconvening Board. Board meeting should include: (a) fairness opinion presentation; (b) management strategic rationale presentation; (c) legal counsel fiduciary duties presentation; (d) approval of all material terms (price, structure, conditions, MAE definition, indemnification). | Signing | MSWC Board + Management + Financial Advisor + Legal Counsel | Day 0 (Board meeting scheduled 1-2 weeks after merger agreement substantially negotiated) |
| 2 | **Proxy Statement Preparation and Mailing**: Prepare proxy materials including: (a) notice of stockholder meeting; (b) merger agreement or fair summary; (c) fairness opinion; (d) risk factors (including environmental disclosure per Section E.2(i) above); (e) board recommendation; (f) appraisal rights notice per DGCL § 262. Delaware M&A counsel reviews proxy for 5-10 days; printing and mailing adds 5-7 days. | Post-Signing | MSWC Legal + Disclosure Counsel + Proxy Solicitation Firm | Days 0-30 (proxy preparation and mailing completed within 30 days of board approval) |
| 3 | **20-Day Notice Period**: DGCL § 251(c) mandates minimum 20 days between proxy mailing and stockholder meeting. This is a strict requirement—courts have invalidated votes where notice was only 19 days. The 20-day period protects stockholders' right to review materials and perfect appraisal rights under § 262. | Proxy Mailing | Automatic (statutory waiting period) | Days 30-50 (stockholders receive proxy materials and 20-day review period elapses) |
| 4 | **Stockholder Meeting and Vote**: Stockholders vote on merger approval. DGCL § 251(c) requires majority of outstanding voting stock (not merely majority of shares present). For example, if MSWC has 100M shares outstanding and 80M present at meeting, approval requires 50M+ votes in favor (majority of 100M outstanding), not merely 40M+ (majority of 80M present). Abstentions and broker non-votes count against the transaction. | Stockholder Meeting Date | MSWC Stockholders + Proxy Solicitation Firm (vote tabulation) | Day 50 (stockholder meeting held on noticed date) |
| 5 | **Certificate of Merger Filing**: After stockholder approval, surviving corporation (typically AWI or merger subsidiary) files certificate of merger with Delaware Secretary of State including: (a) merger agreement or certificate containing material terms; (b) evidence of stockholder approval; (c) effective time (immediate or specified future time); (d) filing fee ($180,300 for $2.4B transaction = $50K base + $130.3K value-based). Certificate can specify effectiveness on future closing date rather than immediately upon filing, coordinating merger effectiveness with funding and closing deliveries. | Stockholder Approval | AWI Legal Counsel + Delaware Registered Agent | Days 50-60 (certificate filed 1-10 days after stockholder approval; effectiveness coordinated with closing date) |
| 6 | **CPUC Approval Coordination**: While Delaware stockholder approval takes 50-70 days, CPUC utility transfer approval takes 9-12 months per Section IV.H. MSWC should coordinate timelines to avoid gap period where: (a) stockholders have approved merger; (b) CPUC approval is pending; (c) no-shop covenant prevents MSWC from soliciting alternatives; (d) AWI can terminate on MAE but MSWC lacks exit options. Recommendation: delay Delaware stockholder vote until CPUC approval is substantially complete (e.g., hold stockholder vote in Month 10-11 when CPUC approval is expected Month 12), minimizing gap period risk. | Throughout Transaction | Both Parties + Regulatory Counsel | Months 1-12 (CPUC approval runs concurrently with Delaware process but takes longer; coordinate stockholder vote timing to minimize gap risk) |

#### E.4 Counter-Party Response Anticipation and Negotiation Strategy

| # | Issue | AWI's Anticipated Position | MSWC's Counter-Position | Negotiation Strategy & Target Outcome |
|---|-------|----------------------------|-------------------------|--------------------------------------|
| 1 | **Environmental Disclosure in Proxy Statement** | AWI will demand that MSWC's proxy statement include generic environmental disclosure ("the Company faces environmental compliance obligations") without quantification, to minimize stockholder litigation risk and avoid highlighting negative information that could cause stockholders to vote down the transaction. | MSWC should insist on detailed quantified disclosure per Section E.2(i) above ($25M-$50M RCRA, $150M-$230M PFAS, $1.4B-$1.95B lead lines) because: (a) Delaware fiduciary duty requires disclosure of severity, not merely categories (*IRA Trust v. Crane*, *In re Volcano Corp.*); (b) inadequate disclosure creates 40-60% stockholder litigation risk per Finding B.1, exposing MSWC directors to personal liability; (c) disclosure defects may breach MSWC's merger agreement representation that proxy materials are accurate and complete, creating indemnification exposure. | **Target:** MSWC includes quantified environmental disclosure in proxy statement per Section E.2(i), and AWI agrees that such disclosure satisfies MSWC's merger agreement obligations. **Fallback:** If AWI insists on generic disclosure, MSWC should demand that AWI indemnify MSWC for stockholder litigation resulting from inadequate proxy disclosure, shifting risk to AWI. |
| 2 | **MAE Definition - Environmental Carve-Out Caps** | AWI will propose either: (a) no environmental carve-out at all, leaving MSWC exposed to MAE termination if any environmental costs exceed projections; or (b) very low caps ($50M-$100M CapEx, $100M-$150M CPUC disallowances, 10,000 customer connections) that effectively give AWI MAE rights for routine environmental compliance. | MSWC should insist on capped carve-out per Section E.2(ii) with $200M/24-month CapEx cap, $300M cumulative CPUC disallowance cap, and 25,000 customer connection disruption cap. MSWC should argue that: (a) these caps are calibrated to the disclosed environmental liabilities ($175M-$280M near-term CapEx, $170M-$600M expected CPUC disallowances); (b) costs within disclosed ranges were "known risks" priced into the $2.4B consideration per *IBP* precedent; (c) only costs materially exceeding disclosed estimates constitute "unknown risks" triggering MAE. | **Opening Position:** $250M CapEx cap / $350M disallowance cap / 30,000 connections (10% cushion above disclosed estimates). **Target Position:** $200M CapEx / $300M disallowance / 25,000 connections (Section E.2(ii) language). **Walk-Away:** $150M CapEx / $200M disallowance / 15,000 connections (below disclosed estimates, making carve-out illusory—at this point, MSWC should reject the transaction or demand $100M-$200M purchase price increase to compensate for assuming environmental risk). **Trade-Off:** If AWI insists on lower caps, MSWC can offer to escrow $100M of purchase price for 36 months, with AWI drawing from escrow if environmental CapEx exceeds $200M—this shifts risk allocation from termination rights (binary outcome favoring AWI) to post-closing escrow adjustment (graduated risk-sharing). |
| 3 | **Proxy Statement "Fundamental Representation" Designation** | AWI will demand that MSWC's representation regarding proxy statement accuracy (Section E.2(iii), subclause (iii)) be designated a "fundamental representation" with: (a) unlimited survival (no 18-24 month survival period); (b) no basket (first-dollar indemnification); (c) no cap (unlimited indemnification). This gives AWI indemnification rights if proxy disclosure is deficient, even if deficiency does not result in stockholder litigation. | MSWC should resist "fundamental representation" designation and instead propose: (a) 24-month survival period (consistent with other non-fundamental representations); (b) $5M basket (materiality threshold before indemnification applies); (c) $50M cap (consistent with general indemnification cap). MSWC should argue that proxy disclosure defects resulting in actual stockholder litigation are already compensable under Delaware fiduciary duty law, and AWI should not receive windfall indemnification for technical disclosure defects that cause no harm. | **Opening Position:** Standard representation with 24-month survival, $5M basket, $50M cap. **Target Position:** Fundamental representation (unlimited survival, no cap) BUT only for disclosure defects that result in actual stockholder litigation with damages >$1M (i.e., AWI must prove harm before indemnification applies). **Walk-Away:** If AWI insists on fundamental representation with no harm requirement, MSWC should demand deletion of the representation entirely, relying solely on Delaware common law fiduciary duty obligations. **Trade-Off:** MSWC can agree to fundamental representation in exchange for AWI's agreement to share defense costs 50/50 if stockholder litigation arises (reducing MSWC's exposure from 100% defense costs to 50%). |
| 4 | **Stockholder Vote Failure - Repeat Vote vs. Termination** | AWI will likely propose that if MSWC's stockholders vote down the merger at the first stockholder meeting, AWI has immediate termination rights without obligation to wait for a second vote. This protects AWI from being locked into a transaction that stockholders oppose. | MSWC should insist on the two-vote structure in Section E.2(iii), subclause (iv): if the first vote fails, MSWC gets 30 days to address stockholder concerns (enhanced disclosure, price increase, improved terms) and hold a second vote. This gives MSWC a second chance to salvage the transaction and avoids immediate termination based on a single vote that may reflect inadequate disclosure rather than genuine opposition to the deal terms. | **Target:** Two-vote structure with 30-day cure period between votes. **Fallback:** If AWI insists on immediate termination rights after first vote failure, MSWC should demand that AWI pay a $50M-$80M reverse termination fee if AWI terminates after first vote failure (compensating MSWC for lost alternative opportunities and sunk transaction costs). **Walk-Away:** If AWI insists on immediate termination with no reverse termination fee, MSWC should propose that the merger agreement automatically terminates after first vote failure with no penalty to either party, allowing both parties to walk away and pursue alternatives. |
